<Text>I am very happy that I joined The Arena last September (2018). Sure, it doesn't smell so pretty ...there is grunting, groaning, sweat on the ground (ugh).  But there is true instruction, learning and growing on every level that is happening everyday.  What they invest in is the coaches, students, fighters and the staff.  Not the fluff.

The gym is wonderfully diverse with many different cultures and backgrounds.  You will immediately see that when you walk in.  So you will never feel like you are "different" or that others will not accept you.  You will also need to make the effort to join in.  No hand holding here.

Of course, The Arena is not for everyone.  So I suggest that you set up an appointment for a tour and maybe take a class.  Have your list of questions and concerns.  They will honestly answer those questions/concerns and will not force or guilt you to join like other places do.  It is your choice.</Text><UserId.>100883341419385467208<//UserId.>< rating>

As a first time student in MMA, The Arena welcomed me with a free trial to see their classes and what they offer. I must say I was beyond impressed during my first day and felt very welcomed by the coaches, staff, and members of the gym. Alex Fanning< /username>
<time>1543680970250<//time><rate>4< /rate>< text>
The Arena's facilities, instructors and classes are absolutely the best in the San Diego area. Very professional and friendly, even with some of the larger class sizes the instructors will do their best to pay attention to everyone, regardless of skill level. This being said, I would advise that you only sign up if you are serious about MMA training, and know that you will attend enough classes for the monthly cost to be worth it, and that you will be staying in the area for a while. Definitely take advantage of the 30 day trial and don't let them sell you on a membership until you are certain that you'll be able to get in there often enough and that it is something you want to pursue. The management system/company they use for membership is a bear to deal with when cancelling a membership. The Arena itself requires a 30 day notice of cancellation, which is fine. However, the management company requires hard-copy proof that you are leaving the area of the gym, and they want you to mail it to them at some odd location where they are based. There is no way to do this online, the Arena can not do it for you at their location. I understand that this system is in place to protect the gym from flakes/frauds/dishonest people that would probably sign up and quit like crazy if they had the opportunity, but it does make it difficult for folks like me that just turned out not to have the time or energy at the end of the day to make it in on a regular basis.< /text>

<userid>100266622857143833789</userid>< review>
This gym is amazing if you plan on competing in any combat sport, or if you're looking for real self-defense ability. The instruction for each discipline is great. Brazilian jiu-jitsu, boxing, muay thai/kickboxing, judo, mma, etc. They probably have the most available classes w/the largest variety of combat sports of any gym in San Diego. The instruction is all quality too. Its a fighters gym, so there's plenty of guys there who will test you & help you get better as you're learning as well.

Many other gyms with cardio kickboxing type programs may have legit technical classes too, but the clientele they attract aren't always the type to test you that you'd be able to defend yourself in real situations. HOWEVER, some do also have those tough individuals while also offering more amenities. For example, this gym does not have full locker rooms/showers, nor saunas, or those supplemental beneficial classes like yoga. It's purely combat, which is not good or bad, it just is.

They are pretty expensive though. You could say they have that cost because of the amount of available classes, but the average person will only train 3 disciplines. Other gyms, nearby too, have many of the same classes & quality- in addition to having a sauna & locker rooms. It all comes down to instructor preference & what you can afford. I like these instructors & students, so I stay.<//review>

<userid>100266622857143833789</userid><Name>Sergio Benitez</Name><Date>1558468967189< /Date>< Rate>

<Text>This gym is amazing if you plan on competing in any combat sport, or if you're looking for real self-defense ability. The instruction for each discipline is great. Brazilian jiu-jitsu, boxing, muay thai/kickboxing, judo, mma, etc. They probably have the most available classes w/the largest variety of combat sports of any gym in San Diego. The instruction is all quality too. Its a fighters gym, so there's plenty of guys there who will test you & help you get better as you're learning as well.

Many other gyms with cardio kickboxing type programs may have legit technical classes too, but the clientele they attract aren't always the type to test you that you'd be able to defend yourself in real situations. HOWEVER, some do also have those tough individuals while also offering more amenities. For example, this gym does not have full locker rooms/showers, nor saunas, or those supplemental beneficial classes like yoga. It's purely combat, which is not good or bad, it just is.

They are pretty expensive though. You could say they have that cost because of the amount of available classes, but the average person will only train 3 disciplines. Other gyms, nearby too, have many of the same classes & quality- in addition to having a sauna & locker rooms. It all comes down to instructor preference & what you can afford. I like these instructors & students, so I stay.<//Text>< pics>

Moved to San Diego 1 month ago. First thing on my list (after moving out of my car into an apartment) was to find the local Jiu Jitsu & MMA schools. Literally drove around San Diego, and checked out half of the gyms in town.. The focus in alot of the gyms is on the egos/images of the staff members VS producing competent fighters, and providing the most efficient & suitable environment for like minded people to meet, and improve towards higher versions of themselves (most of the places you get plenty of mad-dogging, douchiness, etc)....

"THE ARENA" embodies all the complete opposite qualities.. The focus is where it should be, on the training itself.. Not on how many new membership commissions staff members can pull off in a given day or week.. Mike is a great guy. The place beams positive vibes in & out VS all the passive aggressive posturing stuff. Chris Leben is one of the coaches which speaks for itself. He can choose where he wants to work, and yet he works at "THE ARENA".

Am so stoked, and grateful to have found a new home in San Diego that can facilitate me to grow into the person I've always been intending to become.

This place is awesome all around. Siskel & ebert would have given two thumbs up if they were into man stuff. Total win all around.</review>

< Review>
Herbert's beach is one of my favorites. The dogs there are lovely, and their humans are relatively polite. The slough is nasty, (DO NOT GO IN THE POOP WATER) but as long as you keep yourself out of it, it won't bother you (unless provoked). Seagulls are plentiful in case you're feeling peckish (no pun intended. Puns hurt feelings. I don't believe in hurting feelings.). The restaurant smells good, but I only ate there once when I was like 10 so my standards were low and I just had pancakes so I'm actually not sure whether their food is decent or not. Overall rating is an F for 'five-star'.</Review>

< Text>
I should be clear, this is for the Boathouse Restaurant: I've been coming here for many years, and this was the best experience I have had. We were anxious when we arrived as the beach and the restaurant were packed, and a lot of folks weren't wearing masks. However within 20 minutes (the exact wait time we were told to expect), we were lucky enough to be seated outside the patio area along the walk in front of the restaurant, well separated from other tables and people. We had a surprisingly good, interesting cocktail, followed by an amazing seafood platter...the middle size was perfect for 2 for a meal, and everything was very fresh and delicious. A lot of variety as well...clams, mussels, oysters, shrimp, crab legs, ceviche, poke. My only very small complaint was the amount of lettuce/cabbage the ceviche sat on in proportion to the amount of ceviche. While it is not inexpensive, I did think it was fairly priced for the quality and quantity. Their wine selection was quite good, with some nice and unexpected local selections. We had a favorite Sauvignon Blanc from a relatively small producer and it was surprisingly reasonably priced. I appreciate this; knowing a bit about wine and retail costs, i get very frustrated when restaurants jack up the prices unreasonably high... it's the difference between them selling me a glass or a bottle, so worth keeping the prices appropriate.  The service was really good...our server was experienced, very polite and warm but professional. She was knowledgeable about the menu, and when asked, she articulately expressed her opinions, which I VERY much appreciate in a server who really knows the menu. She guided us perfectly. We also didn't feel rushed despite it being a fairly busy evening. Quite honestly, I've always come here for the location in the past, but after this experience I will be returning more frequently for the food and beverages. Overall an outstanding experience.<//Text>

<text>I grew up near here and spent a lot of time at Hendry's as a kid.  Now i spend a lot of time here with my own children.  We love it here....our "locals" beach.  Also known as The Pit to a of us long time Santa Barbarans.  One side is off leash dog friendly the other is on leash walking.  Lots of tidepools at low tide.  Parking cam definitely be a challenge especially on a beautiful day.  There is a restaurant ( The Boathouse) on this beach which also makes parking a challenge.  Famy friendly beach.  It does get crowded at times but you can usually find a spot even on the most crowded days.  Can be foggy from time to time eben when there is no fog anywhere else.  Can usually see dolphins out in the water, birds diving for fish, etc.  A great local hangout!</text>< Pics>

< review>
About 2 weeks ago I was with my family and we were driving from Idaho to California to visit other relatives. We made it to Orange County just fine however, on our way up to Santa Rosa our alternator went out and we eventually had to pull off to the side of the road. After dealing with AAA we were towed to Pete's Auto Repair. From here we met Pedro where he stated that he'd have our alternator fixed in the morning. With no Taxi available, Pedro also offered to give us a ride to a nearby hotel. Turns out that the only hotel nearby wasn't available at that moment because the owner left a note stating they were in the shower. Pedro drove us from Newman, California to Patterson, California which was 20 miles away. From there he made sure we got a Hotel which we did at the Best Western and in the morning he picked us up and drove us back to the repair shop where the alternator was working good as new and the cost was extremely cheap! We drove all the way back to Idaho that day and made it home safely. Pedro you are the man! And Pete's auto repair is an outstanding place!<//review>

< Text>
The memories were worth way  more than the price we paid to rent this boat.  $220 / 5 hours  for  Priceless family adventure.
I was able to enjoy a glass of wine while my son drove me around the lake.
We  rented a  10 passenger pontoon boat from camp Edison marina on a Friday afternoon in June  and it was an absolute perfect day. We took aboard 2 ice chests, 4 kids, & 3 adults. The day use area has alot of lakeside  picnic tables and the tress kept the area cool and  shaded.
Yes of course we cut the engine and  anchored in the center of the Lake for a quik 15 minute dip. It was hot and the cool water felt good. Usually I don't have a problem swimming back to the boat, but HERE  I did . There seemed to be a "different kind of under current" going on. For years we would launch and  swim in cottonwood cove (Colorado river). The depth there is more than  100 feet , Shaver Lake depth was only 50 feet, yet I had more difficulty swimming back over to  the boat? The water isn't the  cleanest , but  it didn't leave a "fishy " smell on us, our clothes or towels .
IMPORTANT NOTE :
USE BUG SPRAY
I didn't realize til next day when I kept scratching and scratching how many clusters of  mosquito  bites I had on my exposed body.
*** THIS BOAT HAD ALOT OF COMFORTABLE SPACE FOR ALL 7 OF US.< /Text>

Good smartphone iphone and ipad repair shop

Came here Jan '16 to repair a broken screen on an iphone 6. I was helping out a friend and needed to have this taken care of on short notice.

Overall everything worked out well. I walked in without an appointment, got quoted the cost ahead of time $109 including tax, and 15 mins. Everything was delivered as requested. They are probably the best and cheapest iphone repair and ipad screen repair shop in los angeles.

Service was very good. I appreciated that the rep / repairman was thorough in testing out different functions of the phone in front of me, before and after the repair. He even went over things that didn't seem related like the audio and aux input outlet.

Furthermore, the repair area is right in the open and you can see them work on your phone, should it be any relief to who care.

The only thing I didnt care so much for was the higher cost of parking in the immediate area, but that's not the fault of the business of course.

With good faith, I will return and send buddies of mine here. Highly Recommended.<//review>

* Back Plate
* Click Wheel

A bargain by any definition!
